formats and generates output files with translated content. For information about text processing and chunking, see [Text Processing](#4.3).\n\n## Overview\n\nThe L2T system supports reading from multiple file formats (plain text and PDF) and writing translated content to text files. The file handling functionality is primarily implemented in the `FileHandler` class, which provides methods for reading input files and writing output files.\n\n```mermaid\nflowchart LR\n    A[\"User Input\"] --\u003e B{\"Is File?\"}\n    B --\u003e|\"Yes\"| C{\"File Type?\"}\n    B --\u003e|\"No\"| D[\"Process as Text String\"]\n    C --\u003e|\"PDF\"| E[\"Extract Text from PDF\"]\n    C --\u003e|\"TXT\"| F[\"Read Text File\"]\n    E --\u003e G[\"File Content\"]\n    F --\u003e G\n    G --\u003e H[\"Translation Engine\"]\n    H --\u003e I[\"Translated Content\"]\n    I --\u003e J{\"Output Destination?\"}\n    J --\u003e|\"Console\"| K[\"Display in Console\"]\n    J --\u003e|\"File\"| L[\"Write to Output File\"]\n```\n\nSources: [app/file_handlers.py:9-53](), [app/cli.py:83-95](), [app/cli.py:154-171]()\n\n## FileHandler Class\n\nThe `FileHandler` class is responsible for all file I/O operations in the L2T system. It provides static methods for reading input files and writing output files.\n\n```mermaid\nclassDiagram\n    class \"FileHandler\" {\n        +read_file(file_path, encoding) str\n        +write_output(content, output_path, encoding) void\n        -_read_pdf(pdf_path) str\n        -_read_text_file(file_path, encoding) str\n    }\n```\n\nSources: [app/file_handlers.py:6-54]()\n\n### Reading Files\n\nThe `FileHandler.read_file()` method is the main entry point for reading files. It determines the file type based on the file extension and delegates to the appropriate reader method:\n\n```mermaid\nflowchart TD\n    A[\"read_file(file_path, encoding)\"] --\u003e B{\"File Type?\"}\n    B --\u003e|\".pdf\"| C[\"_read_pdf(path)\"]\n    B --\u003e|\"other\"| D[\"_read_text_file(path, encoding)\"]\n    C --\u003e E[\"Return Extracted Text\"]\n    D --\u003e E\n```\n\nSources: [app/file_handlers.py:9-19]()\n\n#### Text File Reading\n\nFor text files, the `_read_text_file()` method opens the file with the specified encoding and reads its content. If the encoding is incorrect, it raises a dedicated error message suggesting the user try with a different encoding parameter.\n\nSources: [app/file_handlers.py:34-43]()\n\n#### PDF File Reading\n\nFor PDF files, the `_read_pdf()` method uses the PyPDF2 library to extract text from each page of the document. The extracted text from all pages is then joined with newline characters.\n\nSources: [app/file_handlers.py:21-32]()\n\n### Writing Files\n\nThe `FileHandler.write_output()` method writes the translated content to the specified output file:\n\n```mermaid\nflowchart TD\n    A[\"write_output(content, output_path, encoding)\"] --\u003e B[\"Ensure Parent Directory Exists\"]\n    B --\u003e C[\"Open File with Specified Encoding\"]\n    C --\u003e D[\"Write Content to File\"]\n    D --\u003e E[\"Close File\"]\n```\n\nThis method ensures that the parent directory of the output file exists (creating it if necessary) before writing the content.\n\nSources: [app/file_handlers.py:45-54]()\n\n## Integration with Translation CLI\n\nThe file handling functionality is integrated with the command-line interface through the `TranslationCLI` class.\n\n### Loading Content\n\nThe `_load_content()` method in `TranslationCLI` determines whether the input is a file path or a text string. File Content\"]\n```\n\nSources: [app/cli.py:83-95]()\n\n### Handling Output\n\nThe `_handle_output()` method in `TranslationCLI` determines whether to write the translated content to a file or display it in the console:\n\n```mermaid\nflowchart TD\n    A[\"_handle_output(translated_text)\"] --\u003e B[\"_generate_output_path()\"]\n    B --\u003e C{\"Output Path?\"}\n    C --\u003e|\"Yes\"| D[\"FileHandler.write_output()\"]\n    C --\u003e|\"No\"| E[\"Display in Console\"]\n    D --\u003e F[\"Log Success Message\"]\n```\n\nSources: [app/cli.py:154-171]()\n\n### Output Path Generation\n\nThe `_generate_output_path()` method in `TranslationCLI` generates an output file path based on the input file path and target language:\n\n```mermaid\nflowchart TD\n    A[\"_generate_output_path(input_path)\"] --\u003e B{\"Output Specified?\"}\n    B --\u003e|\"No\"| C{\"Input is File?\"}\n    B --\u003e|\"Yes\"| D[\"Return Specified Output Path\"]\n    C --\u003e|\"Yes\"| E[\"Generate Output Path\"]\n    C --\u003e|\"No\"| F[\"Return None\"]\n    E --\u003e G[\"Construct Path: {input_stem}.{lang_code}.T2L.txt\"]\n```\n\nIf the `-o/--output` option is not specified and the input is a file, the method generates an output file path in the format `{input_filename}.{target_language}.T2L.txt` in the same directory as the input file.\n\nSources: [app/cli.py:172-177]()\n\n## File Format Support\n\nThe following table summarizes the file formats supported by the L2T system:\n\n| Format | Read | Write | Notes |\n|--------|------|-------|-------|\n| Plain Text (.txt) | ✓ | ✓ | Supports custom encoding via -e/--encoding flag |\n| PDF (.pdf) | ✓ | ✗ | Text extraction only, no writing |\n| Other text-based formats | ✓ | ✓ | Treated as plain text |\n\nSources: [app/file_handlers.py:9-19](), [app/file_handlers.py:45-54]()\n\n## Error Handling\n\nThe `FileHandler` class includes robust error handling for various file operations:\n\n1. **File Not Found** - When the specified input file does not exist\n2. **Encoding Errors** - When the specified encoding is incorrect for the input file\n3. **PDF Extraction Errors** - When there are issues extracting text from PDF files\n4. **Write Permission Errors** - When the system cannot write to the specified output location\n\nAll errors are logged and propagated to the calling code with descriptive error messages.\n\nSources: [app/file_handlers.py:18-19](), [app/file_handlers.py:31-32](), [app/file_handlers.py:41-43](), [app/file_handlers.py:53-54]()\n\n## Usage Example\n\nHere's how the file handling component is used in a typical translation workflow:\n\n```mermaid\nsequenceDiagram\n    participant \"User\" as U\n error\"\n```\n\nSources: [app/cli.py:47-66]()\n\n## Implementation Details\n\nThe `FileHandler` class is designed with static methods to provide a stateless API for file operations. This design choice simplifies usage and prevents the need for instantiating objects for simple file operations.\n\nFor PDF files, the system uses PyPDF2 to extract text page by page. This approach ensures that all text content is captured, even if it spans multiple pages. The extracted text from each page is concatenated with newline characters to preserve the document structure.\n\nWhen writing output files, the system automatically creates parent directories if they don't exist, ensuring that users can specify output paths in any location without needing to create the directory structure manually.\n\nSources: [app/file_handlers.py:6-54]()"])</script><script>self.__next_f.push([1,"20:T20c8,"])</script><script>self.__next_f.push([1,"# Text Processing\n\n\u003cdetails\u003e\n\u003csummary\u003eRelevant source files\u003c/summary\u003e\n\nThe following files were used as context for generating this wiki page:\n\n- [app/cli.py](app/cli.py)\n- [app/utils.py](app/utils.py)\n\n\u003c/details\u003e\n\n\n\nThis page documents the text processing subsystem in the L2T application. Text processing in L2T involves breaking down input text into manageable chunks, handling paragraphs appropriately, and preparing content for translation. For information about file handling and input/output operations, see [File Handling](#4.2).\n\n## Overview\n\nThe text processing functionality is primarily handled by the `TextProcessor` class in the utils module. This class provides methods to split and prepare text for efficient translation by the NLLB model.\n\n```mermaid\ngraph TD\n    subgraph \"Text Processing System\"\n        Input[\"Input Text/Content\"] --\u003e TextProcessor[\"TextProcessor Class\"]\n        TextProcessor --\u003e ChunkText[\"chunk_text() Method\"]\n        TextProcessor --\u003e SplitParagraphs[\"split_paragraphs() Method\"]\n        \n        ChunkText --\u003e ChunkedContent[\"Text Divided by Size\"]\n        SplitParagraphs --\u003e ParagraphList[\"Text Divided by Paragraphs\"]\n        \n        ChunkedContent --\u003e Translator[\"Translation Engine\"]\n        ParagraphList --\u003e Translator\n    end\n```\n\nSources: [app/utils.py:22-34]()\n\n## TextProcessor Class\n\nThe `TextProcessor` class is a utility class that serves as the core of the text processing system. It provides static methods for manipulating text:\n\n- `chunk_text()`: Divides text into chunks of a specified size\n- `split_paragraphs()`: Separates text into paragraphs based on newline characters\n\n### Implementation Details\n\n```mermaid\nclassDiagram\n    class TextProcessor {\n        +chunk_text(text: str, chunk_size: int) -\u003e List[str]\n        +split_paragraphs(text: str) -\u003e List[str]\n    }\n```\n\nSources: [app/utils.py:22-34]()\n\n### chunk_text Method\n\nThe `chunk_text` method divides a string into chunks of a specified size:\n\n```python\n@staticmethod\ndef chunk_text(text: str, chunk_size: int) -\u003e List[str]:\n    \"\"\"Découpe un texte en segments de taille fixe.\"\"\"\n    return [text[i:i + chunk_size] for i in range(0, len(text), chunk_size)]\n```\n\nThis method uses a simple list comprehension to create chunks of text, each with a maximum length of `chunk_size`.\n\nSources: [app/utils.py:26-29]()\n\n### split_paragraphs Method\n\nThe `split_paragraphs` method divides text into paragraphs based on newline characters:\n\n```python\n@staticmethod\ndef split_paragraphs(text: str) -\u003e List[str]:\n    \"\"\"Sépare le texte en paragraphes.\"\"\"\n    return [p.strip() for p in text.split('\\n')]\n```\n\nThis method provides a natural way to segment text that preserves the logical structure of the content.\n\nSources: [app/utils.py:31-34]()\n\n## Text Processing Workflow\n\nThe text processing workflow in L2T is determined by the size of the input text:\n\n```mermaid\nflowchart TD\n    Input[\"Input Text\"] --\u003e SizeCheck{\"Text Size \u003c= chunk_size?\"}\n    \n    SizeCheck --\u003e|\"Yes (Small Text)\"| DirectTranslate[\"Direct Translation\"]\n    SizeCheck --\u003e|\"No (Large Text)\"| SplitProcess[\"Process in Chunks\"]\n    \n    SplitProcess --\u003e SplitParagraphs[\"TextProcessor.split_paragraphs()\"]\n    SplitParagraphs --\u003e Paragraphs[\"List of Paragraph Segments\"]\n    \n    Paragraphs --\u003e TranslateLoop[\"Translate Each Segment\"]\n    TranslateLoop --\u003e JoinResults[\"Join Results with '\\\\n'\"]\n    \n    DirectTranslate --\u003e Result[\"Final Translated Text\"]\n    JoinResults --\u003e Result\n```\n\nSources: [app/cli.py:98-120](), [app/cli.py:123-151]()\n\n### Small Text Processing\n\nFor small text inputs (less than or equal to the configured chunk size):\n- The entire text is translated in a single operation\n- No progress tracking is displayed\n- Results are returned directly\n\nSources: [app/cli.py:104-109]()\n\n### Large Text Processing\n\nFor large text inputs:\n1. Text is split into paragraphs using `TextProcessor.split_paragraphs()`\n2. Each paragraph is translated individually\n3. Progress is tracked and displayed using `ProgressHandler.display_progress()`\n4. Empty paragraphs are preserved but not sent to the translator\n5. Results are joined back together with newline characters\n\n```mermaid\nflowchart TD\n    Content[\"Large Text Content\"] --\u003e SplitParagraphs[\"TextProcessor.split_paragraphs()\"]\n    SplitParagraphs --\u003e ParagraphArray[\"Array of Paragraphs\"]\n    \n    ParagraphArray --\u003e ProcessLoop[\"For each paragraph\"]\n    ProcessLoop --\u003e EmptyCheck{\"Is paragraph empty?\"}\n    \n    EmptyCheck --\u003e|\"Yes\"| SkipTranslation[\"Add empty string to results\"]\n    EmptyCheck --\u003e|\"No\"| Translate[\"Translate paragraph\"]\n    \n    SkipTranslation --\u003e UpdateProgress[\"Update progress display\"]\n    Translate --\u003e UpdateProgress\n    \n    UpdateProgress --\u003e NextIteration{\"More paragraphs?\"}\n    NextIteration --\u003e|\"Yes\"| ProcessLoop\n    NextIteration --\u003e|\"No\"| JoinResults[\"Join results with '\\\\n'.join()\"]\n    \n    JoinResults --\u003e FinalText[\"Final translated text\"]\n```\n\nSources: [app/cli.py:123-151]()\n\n## Progress Handling During Text Processing\n\nFor large text processing, L2T implements a progress display mechanism through the `ProgressHandler` class:\n\n```mermaid\ngraph TD\n    Start[\"Start Processing\"] --\u003e Initialize[\"Initialize Progress Tracking\"]\n    Initialize --\u003e Loop[\"Process Each Paragraph\"]\n    \n    Loop --\u003e Check{\"Update Progress?\"}\n    Check --\u003e|\"Yes (i % max(1, total//100) == 0 or i == total)\"| Update[\"ProgressHandler.display_progress()\"]\n    Check --\u003e|\"No\"| NextItem[\"Process Next Item\"]\n    \n    Update --\u003e NextItem\n    NextItem --\u003e More{\"More Items?\"}\n    More --\u003e|\"Yes\"| Loop\n    More --\u003e|\"No\"| End[\"Complete\"]\n```\n\nThe progress display includes:\n- A visual bar showing completion percentage\n- Current/total segments count\n- Elapsed time information\n\nSources: [app/utils.py:5-22](), [app/cli.py:126-151]()\n\n## Performance Considerations\n\n### Chunk Size Impact\n\nThe chunk size parameter (configurable via CLI with `-c/--chunk-size`, default: 500) has significant impact on processing:\n\n| Chunk Size | Advantages | Disadvantages |\n|------------|------------|---------------|\n| Smaller    | - Better memory management\u003cbr\u003e- More granular progress updates | - Higher processing overhead\u003cbr\u003e- More API calls |\n| Larger     | - Fewer translation calls\u003cbr\u003e- Better context for translation | - Higher memory requirements\u003cbr\u003e- Less frequent progress updates |\n\nSources: [app/cli.py:42](), [app/cli.py:104-109]()\n\n### Paragraph-Based Processing\n\nL2T uses paragraphs as the natural processing unit because:\n1. Paragraphs typically contain complete thoughts\n2. Translation quality is better when preserving sentence context\n3. It allows for more intuitive progress tracking\n4. Empty paragraphs can be preserved without sending them to the translator\n\nSources: [app/cli.py:123-151](), [app/utils.py:31-34]()\n\n## Integration with Translation Workflow\n\nText processing is tightly integrated with the translation pipeline:\n\n```mermaid\ngraph TD\n    User[\"User Input\"] --\u003e CLI[\"TranslationCLI.run()\"]\n    CLI --\u003e Load[\"_load_content()\"]\n    Load --\u003e Validate[\"Validate Content\"]\n    \n    Validate --\u003e TranslateContent[\"_translate_content()\"]\n    TranslateContent --\u003e SizeCheck{\"Content Size Check\"}\n    \n    SizeCheck --\u003e|\"Small\"| Direct[\"Direct Translation\"]\n    SizeCheck --\u003e|\"Large\"| Chunked[\"_translate_in_chunks()\"]\n    \n    Chunked --\u003e TextProcessor[\"TextProcessor.split_paragraphs()\"]\n    TextProcessor --\u003e Process[\"Process Each Paragraph\"]\n    Process --\u003e Join[\"Join Results\"]\n    \n    Direct --\u003e Output[\"Translated Output\"]\n    Join --\u003e Output\n    \n    Output --\u003e HandleOutput[\"_handle_output()\"]\n```\n\nSources: [app/cli.py:47-58](), [app/cli.py:98-151]()\n\n## Customizing Text Processing\n\nUsers can customize text processing behavior through the following CLI parameters:\n\n| Parameter | Description | Default |\n|-----------|-------------|---------|\n| `-c`, `--chunk-size` | Size of text segments for processing | 500 |\n| `--batch-size` | Number of segments processed together (GPU) | 8 |\n\nSources: [app/cli.py:42-43]()\n\n## Error Handling\n\nThe text processing subsystem includes several error handling mechanisms:\n\n1. Empty paragraphs are handled gracefully by skipping translation\n2. Failed paragraph translations are marked with `[ERREUR]` and processing continues\n3. Warnings are logged for segment-specific errors\n4. The overall process continues even if individual segments fail\n\nSources: [app/cli.py:134-144]()"])</script><script>self.__next_f.push([1,"21:T1a83,"])</script><script>self.__next_f.push([1,"# Logging and Error Handling\n\n\u003cdetails\u003e\n\u003csummary\u003eRelevant source files\u003c/summary\u003e\n\nThe following files were used as context for generating this wiki page:\n\n- [app/logger.py](app/logger.py)\n- [app/main.py](app/main.py)\n\n\u003c/details\u003e\n\n\n\nThis document describes the logging and error handling mechanisms implemented in the L2T system. It covers how log events are generated, processed, and stored, as well as how exceptions are caught and managed throughout the application execution.\n\nFor information about text processing and chunking, see [Text Processing](#4.3).\n\n## Logging System Overview\n\nThe L2T system implements a comprehensive logging system that captures important events, warnings, and errors during translation operations. The logging system is designed to output messages to both a file and the console, providing visibility into application operations.\n\n```mermaid\nflowchart TD\n    subgraph \"Components\"\n        CLI[\"TranslationCLI\"]\n        Translator[\"NLLBTranslator\"]\n        FileHandlers[\"FileHandler\"]\n        TextProcessor[\"TextProcessor\"]\n    end\n\n    subgraph \"Logging System\"\n ConsoleHandler --\u003e Console\n```\n\n**Diagram: Logging System Architecture**\n\nSources: [app/logger.py:5-24]()\n\n### Logging Configuration\n\nThe logging system is initialized using the `setup_logging()` function, which creates a logger named 'T2L' with the following configuration:\n\n- Log level set to INFO by default\n- Standardized log format: timestamp, log level, and message\n- Dual output to both file and console\n\n```mermaid\nsequenceDiagram\n    participant App as \"Application\"\n    participant Logger as \"setup_logging()\"\n    participant T2L as \"T2L Logger\"\n logger\n```\n\n**Diagram: Logger Initialization Sequence**\n\nSources: [app/logger.py:5-24]()\n\n### Log Execution Time Tracking\n\nThe system includes a utility function `log_execution_time()` to `setup_logging()` | Configure logging system | `log_file`: Path to log file (default: 'translation_log.txt') |\n| `log_execution_time()` | Log duration of operations | `start_time`: Operation start time\u003cbr\u003e`action_name`: Description of the operation |\n\nSources: [app/logger.py:5-29]()\n\n## Error Handling\n\nL2T implements a multi-layered error handling strategy to ensure graceful operation even when problems occur. The main entry point encapsulates the CLI execution in a try-except block to catch and manage exceptions.\n\n```mermaid\nflowchart TD\n    Start[\"Application Start\"] --\u003e Configure[\"Configure Environment\"]\n    Configure --\u003e TryCatch{\"Try-Except Block\"}\n    \n    TryCatch --\u003e CLI[\"Initialize and Run CLI\"]\n    CLI --\u003e Success[\"Successful Completion\"]\n    \n    TryCatch --\u003e |\"KeyboardInterrupt\"| Interrupt[\"Display Interruption Message\"]\n    Interrupt --\u003e Exit0[\"Exit with Code 0\"]\n    \n    TryCatch --\u003e |\"Other Exceptions\"| Error[\"Display Error Message\"]\n    Error --\u003e Exit1[\"Exit with Code 1\"]\n    \n    Success --\u003e End[\"Application End\"]\n    Exit0 --\u003e End\n    Exit1 --\u003e End\n```\n\n**Diagram: Global Error Handling Flow**\n\nSources: [app/main.py:5-17]()\n\n### Exception Types and Handling\n\nThe application handles different types of exceptions:\n\n1. **KeyboardInterrupt**: Gracefully exits when the user interrupts the process (Ctrl+C)\n2. **General Exceptions**: Catches all other exceptions, displays the error message, and exits with a non-zero status code\n\nThis approach ensures that:\n- Users can safely interrupt long-running translations\n- Unexpected errors are displayed clearly rather than producing a stack trace\n- The application always terminates cleanly\n\nSources: [app/main.py:11-16]()\n\n## Integration with Application Components\n\nThe logging system is designed to be used by all components of the L2T system. While the logger is initialized centrally, it's accessed throughout the application using the Python standard logging module.\n\n```mermaid\nclassDiagram\n    class Logger {\n        +setup_logging(log_file) Logger\n        +log_execution_time(start_time, action_name) void\n    }\n    \n    class TranslationCLI {\n        +run() void\n    }\n    \n    class NLLBTranslator {\n        +translate() string\n        +translate_batch() list\n    }\n    \n    class FileHandler {\n        +read_file() string\n        +write_output() void\n    }\n    \n    TranslationCLI --\u003e Logger : logs events\n    NLLBTranslator --\u003e Logger : logs translations\n    FileHandler --\u003e Logger : logs I/O operations\n```\n\n**Diagram: Logger Integration with Components**\n\n## Best Practices for Using the Logging System\n\nWhen interacting with the L2T logging system, follow these guidelines:\n\n1. Use the appropriate log level:\n   - `DEBUG`: Detailed information for troubleshooting\n   - `INFO`: Confirmation that things are working as expected\n   - `WARNING`: An indication that something unexpected happened\n   - `ERROR`: Due to a more serious problem, some functionality couldn't be executed\n   - `CRITICAL`: A serious error that might prevent the program from continuing\n\n2. Include relevant context in log messages:\n   - Source and target languages\n   - File names (without full paths for security)\n   - Operation being performed\n   - Size metrics (number of chunks, characters, etc.)\n\n3. Use `log_execution_time()` for performance-sensitive operations\n\n## Conclusion\n\nThe L2T logging and error handling systems work together to ensure:\n\n1. Visibility into application operations\n2. Persistent record of translation activities\n3. Graceful handling of errors and interruptions\n4. It focuses on techniques used to efficiently process large texts, optimize memory usage, and leverage GPU acceleration for faster translations. For specific details on GPU setup and configuration, see [GPU Acceleration](#5.1).\n\n## Performance Challenges in Translation\n\nThe L2T system addresses several performance challenges inherent to neural machine translation:\n\n- Processing large text documents efficiently\n- Managing memory constraints with language models\n- Optimizing GPU utilization\n- Providing progress feedback for long-running translations\n\n```mermaid\nflowchart TD\n    subgraph \"Performance Challenges\"\n        A[\"Large Text Handling\"]\n        B[\"Memory Management\"]\n        C[\"GPU Utilization\"]\n        D[\"User Experience\"]\n    end\n    \n    subgraph \"Optimization Strategies\"\n        E[\"Text Chunking\"]\n        F[\"Paragraph Splitting\"]\n        G[\"CUDA Optimizations\"]\n        H[\"Batch Processing\"]\n        I[\"Progress Visualization\"]\n    end\n    \n    A --\u003e E\n    A --\u003e F\n    B --\u003e E\n    B --\u003e G\n    C --\u003e G\n    C --\u003e H\n    D --\u003e I\n```\n\nSources: [app/cli.py:104-116](), [app/optimizations.py:15-21]()\n\n## Text Processing Optimizations\n\n### Chunking Strategy\n\nFor efficient processing, L2T implements a size-based chunking strategy that:\n\n1. Determines if a text exceeds the configured chunk size\n2. For small texts (≤ chunk_size), performs direct translation\n3. For large texts, breaks content into manageable paragraphs\n4. Processes each paragraph separately and combines results\n\n```mermaid\nflowchart TD\n    A[\"Input Text\"] --\u003e B{\"Size \u003e Chunk Size?\"}\n    B --\u003e|No| C[\"Direct Translation\"]\n    B --\u003e|Yes| D[\"Split into Paragraphs\"]\n    D --\u003e E[\"Process Each Paragraph\"]\n    E --\u003e F[\"Combine Results\"]\n    C --\u003e G[\"Translated Text\"]\n    F --\u003e G\n```\n\nSources: [app/cli.py:98-119](), [app/utils.py:26-34]()\n\nThe chunk size is configurable through the CLI with the `-c/--chunk-size` parameter, which defaults to 500 characters:\n\n```\n-c, --chunk-size  Taille des segments (default: 500)\n```\n\n### Paragraph Splitting\n\nThe system uses intelligent paragraph splitting instead of arbitrary chunking to preserve context:\n\n```mermaid\nflowchart LR\n    A[\"Full Text\"] --\u003e B[\"TextProcessor.split_paragraphs()\"]\n    B --\u003e C[\"List of Paragraphs\"]\n    C --\u003e D[\"Process Each Paragraph\"]\n    D --\u003e E[\"Join with Newlines\"]\n    E --\u003e F[\"Final Translation\"]\n```\n\nSources: [app/cli.py:125-126](), [app/utils.py:31-34]()\n\n## Memory Management\n\nLarge translation models require efficient memory management:\n\n1. The system uses a custom `TranslationDataset` class for optimized data loading\n2. For large texts, content is processed in segments to prevent out-of-memory errors\n3. GPU memory is explicitly cleared with `torch.cuda.empty_cache()`\n\n```mermaid\nclassDiagram\n    class TranslationDataset {\n        texts\n        __len__()\n        __getitem__(idx)\n    }\n    \n    class DataLoader {\n        dataset\n        batch_size\n        shuffle\n    }\n    \n    TranslationDataset --\u003e DataLoader: feeds into\n```\n\nSources: [app/optimizations.py:4-13](), [app/optimizations.py:20-21]()\n\n## GPU Acceleration\n\n### CUDA Configuration\n\nThe system automatically configures the PyTorch environment for optimal GPU performance:\n\n```mermaid\nflowchart TD\n    A[\"configure_environment()\"] --\u003e B[\"Set cudnn.benchmark = True\"]\n    A --\u003e C[\"Set float32_matmul_precision = 'high'\"]\n    A --\u003e D{\"CUDA Available?\"}\n    D --\u003e|Yes| E[\"Clear CUDA Cache\"]\n```\n\nSources: [app/optimizations.py:15-21]()\n\n### Batch Processing\n\nTranslation performance is optimized through batch processing:\n\n1. The batch size is configurable through the CLI with `--batch-size` parameter\n2. Default batch size is 8, which provides a good balance for most GPU configurations\n3. Larger batch sizes can improve throughput on high-end GPUs\n\n```\n--batch-size  Taille des batchs GPU (default: 8)\n```\n\nSources: [app/cli.py:42]()\n\n## Progress Tracking for Large Translations\n\nFor lengthy translation tasks, L2T implements a robust progress tracking system:\n\n```mermaid\nsequenceDiagram\n    participant User\n    participant CLI as \"TranslationCLI\"\n    participant Progress as \"ProgressHandler\"\n    participant Translator as \"NLLBTranslator\"\n    \n    User-\u003e\u003eCLI: Launch translation\n    CLI-\u003e\u003eCLI: Split text into paragraphs\n    CLI-\u003e\u003eProgress: display_progress(0, total, start_time)\n    \n    loop For each paragraph\n        CLI-\u003e\u003eTranslator: translate(paragraph)\n        Translator--\u003e\u003eCLI: translated paragraph\n        CLI-\u003e\u003eProgress: display_progress(i, total, start_time)\n    end\n    \n    CLI-\u003e\u003eUser: Display final result\n```\n\nThe progress display shows:\n- Percentage completion\n- Visual bar representation\n- Current/total segment count\n- Elapsed time\n\nSources: [app/cli.py:130-148](), [app/utils.py:5-21]()\n\n## Performance Optimization Flow\n\nThe complete optimization flow in L2T combines multiple strategies:\n\n```mermaid\nflowchart TD\n    A[\"User Input\"] --\u003e B[\"TranslationCLI._translate_content()\"]\n    \n    B --\u003e C{\"Text Size Check\"}\n    C --\u003e|Small Text| D[\"Direct Translation\"]\n    C --\u003e|Large Text| E[\"TextProcessor.split_paragraphs()\"]\n    \n    E --\u003e F[\"Start Progress Tracking\"]\n    F --\u003e G[\"Process Paragraphs in Loop\"]\n    \n    G --\u003e H[\"NLLBTranslator.translate()\"]\n    H --\u003e I[\"Update Progress\"]\n    I --\u003e J{\"More Paragraphs?\"}\n    J --\u003e|Yes| G\n    J --\u003e|No| K[\"Join Results\"]\n    \n    D --\u003e L[\"Return Translation\"]\n    K --\u003e L\n```\n\nSources: [app/cli.py:98-119](), [app/cli.py:123-151]()\n\n## Performance Recommendations\n\nFor optimal performance with L2T:\n\n| Scenario | Recommended Settings |\n|----------|---------------------|\n| Small texts (\u003c 5KB) | Default settings |\n| Medium texts (5-50KB) | `--chunk-size 1000 --batch-size 8` |\n| Large texts (\u003e 50KB) | `--chunk-size 500 --batch-size 16` (with 8GB+ VRAM) |\n| Limited GPU memory | `--chunk-size 250 --batch-size 4` |\n| High-end GPU (16GB+ VRAM) | `--chunk-size 2000 --batch-size 32` |\n\nSources: [app/cli.py:41-43]()\n\n## Monitoring and Optimization Techniques\n\nThe system uses various techniques to monitor and optimize performance:\n\n1. **Execution Time Logging**: Records and logs total execution time using `log_execution_time()`\n2. **Selective Progress Updates**: Updates progress display selectively to minimize overhead:\n   ```python\n   if i % max(1, total//100) == 0 or i == total:  # 100 updates max\n       ProgressHandler.display_progress(i, total, start_time)\n   ```\n3. **Empty Paragraph Handling**: Skips processing for empty paragraphs to save computation time\n4. **Error Recovery**: Continues processing despite individual paragraph translation failures\n\nSources: [app/cli.py:66](), [app/cli.py:147-148](), [app/cli.py:133-137](), [app/cli.py:138-144]()\n\n## Technical Implementation\n\nThe performance optimization system is implemented through several interconnected components:\n\n```mermaid\nclassDiagram\n    class TranslationCLI {\n        +_translate_content(content)\n        +_translate_in_chunks(content)\n    }\n    \n    class NLLBTranslator {\n        +translate(text, target_lang, source_lang)\n    }\n    \n    class TextProcessor {\n        +split_paragraphs(text)\n        +chunk_text(text, chunk_size)\n    }\n    \n    class ProgressHandler {\n        +display_progress(current, total, start_time)\n    }\n    \n    class configure_environment {\n        +torch.backends.cudnn.benchmark = True\n        +torch.set_float32_matmul_precision('high')\n        +torch.cuda.empty_cache()\n    }\n    \n    TranslationCLI --\u003e TextProcessor: uses\n    TranslationCLI --\u003e ProgressHandler: uses\n    TranslationCLI --\u003e NLLBTranslator: uses\n    NLLBTranslator --\u003e configure_environment: calls\n```\n\nSources: [app/cli.py:14-177](), [app/optimizations.py:1-21](), Clears CUDA cache before loading models:\n   ```python\n   torch.cuda.empty_cache()\n   ```\n\n2. Processes text in manageable chunks to control memory usage\n\n3. Uses batch processing to optimize throughput while respecting memory limits\n\nSources: [app/optimizations.py:20-21](), [gpu/gpu_sync.py:5]()\n\n## Performance Comparison\n\nTranslation performance with and without GPU acceleration varies significantly:\n\n| Text Size | CPU Only | With GPU Acceleration | Speedup |\n|-----------|---------|----------------------|---------|\n| Small (\u003c 1KB) | Minimal difference | Minimal difference | 1-2x |\n| Medium (1-100KB) | Moderate | Good improvement | 3-5x |\n| Large (\u003e 100KB) | Slow | Significant improvement | 5-10x+ |\n\nThe actual speedup depends on your specific GPU model, with more powerful GPUs providing greater acceleration benefits.\n\nSources: [gpu/gpu_sync.py:2-14](), [app/optimizations.py:15-21]()"])</script><script>self.__next_f.push([1,"24:T26c5,"])</script><script>self.__next_f.push([1,"# Sample Files and Testing\n\n\u003cdetails\u003e\n\u003csummary\u003eRelevant source files\u003c/summary\u003e\n\nThe following files were used as context for generating this wiki page:\n\n- [app/minimal/README.md](app/minimal/README.md)\n- [docs/Le_Lievre_et_la_Tortue.txt](docs/Le_Lievre_et_la_Tortue.txt)\n- [docs/Le_Petit_Prince_ASE.eng-Latn.T2L.txt](docs/Le_Petit_Prince_ASE.eng-Latn.T2L.txt)\n- [docs/Le_Petit_Prince_ASE.pdf](docs/Le_Petit_Prince_ASE.pdf)\n\n\u003c/details\u003e\n\n\n\nThis document provides a detailed guide to the sample files included in the L2T repository and explains how to use them for testing the translation system. It covers the location and purpose of sample files, testing methodologies, and common test scenarios to validate the system's functionality.\n\nFor information about developing new features or modifying the system, see [Development Guidelines](#7).\n\n## 1. Overview of Sample Files\n\nThe L2T repository includes several sample files designed to test various aspects of the translation system. These files serve multiple purposes:\n\n1. **Demonstration** - Show the capabilities of the translation system with real-world examples\n2. **Testing** - Provide standardized content for testing translation accuracy and performance\n3. **Validation** - Enable verification of system functionality after code changes\n\n### 1.1 Sample File Locations and Types\n\n```mermaid\nflowchart LR\n    root[\"Repository Root\"]\n    docs[\"docs/ Directory\"]\n    minimal[\"app/minimal/ Directory\"]\n    \n    root --\u003e docs\n    root --\u003e minimal\n    \n    docs --\u003e source[\"Source Text Files (.txt)\"]\n    docs --\u003e translated[\"Translated Files (.T2L.txt)\"]\n    \n    minimal --\u003e readme[\"README.md (Usage Examples)\"]\n    minimal --\u003e testScripts[\"Test Scripts (test-nllb.py)\"]\n    minimal --\u003e cliScripts[\"CLI Scripts (cli-nllb.py)\"]\n    \n    source --\u003e frenchTexts[\"French Literary Texts\n    (Le_Lievre_et_la_Tortue.txt)\"]\n    \n    translated --\u003e englishTexts[\"English Translations\n    (Le_Petit_Prince_ASE.eng-Latn.T2L.txt)\"]\n```\n\nSources: `docs/Le_Lievre_et_la_Tortue.txt`, `docs/Le_Petit_Prince_ASE.eng-Latn.T2L.txt`, `app/minimal/README.md`\n\n### 1.2 Sample File Naming Conventions\n\nThe L2T system follows specific naming conventions for sample files:\n\n- **Source files**: Original filenames (e.g., `Le_Lievre_et_la_Tortue.txt`)\n- **Translated files**: Original filename + language code + `.T2L.txt` extension (e.g., `Le_Petit_Prince_ASE.eng-Latn.T2L.txt`)\n\nThe language code follows the NLLB-200 model's format, which uses ISO codes with script designations (e.g., `eng_Latn` for English in Latin script).\n\nSources: `docs/Le_Petit_Prince_ASE.eng-Latn.T2L.txt`\n\n## 2. Available Sample Files\n\n### 2.1 Literary Texts\n\nThe repository includes classical literary texts that showcase the system's ability to handle complex, nuanced language:\n\n| Filename | Language | Description | Line Count |\n|----------|----------|-------------|------------|\n| `Le_Lievre_et_la_Tortue.txt` | French | La Fontaine's fable \"The Hare and the Tortoise\" | 50 lines |\n| `Le_Petit_Prince_ASE.eng-Latn.T2L.txt` | English (translated) | English translation of \"The Little Prince\" by Saint-Exupéry | 1,872+ lines |\n\nThese files are particularly useful for testing:\n- Literary translation quality\n- Handling of idiomatic expressions\n- Preservation of style and tone\n- Translation of cultural references\n\nSources: `docs/Le_Lievre_et_la_Tortue.txt`, `docs/Le_Petit_Prince_ASE.eng-Latn.T2L.txt`\n\n## 3. Testing Utilities\n\nThe L2T system provides several utilities for testing translation functionality:\n\n```mermaid\nflowchart TD\n    user[\"User\"]\n    testNLLB[\"test-nllb.py\n    Basic Model Testing\"]\n    cliNLLB[\"cli-nllb.py\n    Command-line Interface\"]\n    \n    user --\u003e|\"Run simple test\"| testNLLB\n    user --\u003e|\"Test with options\"| cliNLLB\n    \n    testNLLB --\u003e|\"Loads\"| model[\"NLLB-200 Translation Model\"]\n    cliNLLB --\u003e|\"Loads\"| model\n    \n    model --\u003e|\"Translates\"| output[\"Translation Output\"]\n    \n    output --\u003e|\"Console output\"| console[\"Console Display\"]\n    output --\u003e|\"File output\"| file[\"Generated .T2L.txt File\"]\n    \n    subgraph \"Testing Components\"\n        testNLLB\n        cliNLLB\n    end\n    \n    subgraph \"Core System\"\n        model\n    end\n    \n    subgraph \"Output Options\"\n        console\n        file\n    end\n```\n\nSources: `app/minimal/README.md`\n\n### 3.1 Basic Testing Script\n\nThe `test-nllb.py` script provides a simple way to test the core translation functionality with a default \"Hello World\" test case:\n\n```bash\nuv run test-nllb.py\n```\n\nThis script:\n1. Loads the NLLB-200 model\n2. Translates a simple test phrase\n3. Displays the result in the console\n\nSources: `app/minimal/README.md:7-10`\n\n### 3.2 Command-Line Interface\n\nThe `cli-nllb.py` script offers a more flexible interface with various options:\n\n```bash\nuv run cli-nllb.py \"Traduit ce texte\" -t eng_Latn\n```\n\nThis command translates the French text \"Traduit ce texte\" to English using the NLLB-200 model.\n\nSources: `app/minimal/README.md:11-14`\n\n## 4. Testing Workflows\n\n### 4.1 Text File Translation Testing\n\nThe following diagram illustrates the process of testing translation using sample text files:\n\n```mermaid\nsequenceDiagram\n    participant User\n    participant CLI as \"TranslationCLI\"\n    participant Translator as \"NLLBTranslator\"\n    participant FileHandler as \"FileHandler\"\n    \n    User-\u003e\u003eCLI: Invoke with text file path\n    CLI-\u003e\u003eFileHandler: Read file\n    FileHandler--\u003e\u003eCLI: Return content\n    CLI-\u003e\u003eTranslator: Translate content\n    Translator--\u003e\u003eCLI: Return translation\n    CLI-\u003e\u003eFileHandler: Write output file\n    FileHandler--\u003e\u003eUser: Create .T2L.txt file\n```\n\nFor example, to test translation of the included French fable:\n\n```bash\nuv run cli-nllb.py docs/Le_Lievre_et_la_Tortue.txt -l eng_Latn\n```\n\nThis command:\n1. Reads the French text from `docs/Le_Lievre_et_la_Tortue.txt`\n2. Translates it to English using the NLLB-200 model\n3. Creates an output file `docs/Le_Lievre_et_la_Tortue.eng-Latn.T2L.txt`\n\nSources: `docs/Le_Lievre_et_la_Tortue.txt`, `app/minimal/README.md`\n\n### 4.2 File Format Testing\n\nThe sample files also enable testing of different file formats and encodings. The system supports:\n\n- Plain text files (`.txt`)\n- PDF documents (extracted text)\n- Various encodings (UTF-8, etc.)\n\n## 5. Performance Testing\n\nThe sample files provide standardized content for performance testing:\n\n### 5.1 Translation Speed Testing\n\nLarger files like `Le_Petit_Prince_ASE.eng-Latn.T2L.txt` can be used to measure:\n- Translation speed (tokens/second)\n- Memory usage during translation\n- Chunk processing efficiency\n\n### 5.2 Testing with Different Model Parameters\n\nThe translation system supports various model parameters that can be tested using sample files:\n\n| Parameter | Description | Testing Impact |\n|-----------|-------------|----------------|\n| Chunk Size | Size of text segments processed at once | Affects memory usage and translation coherence |\n| Batch Size | Number of chunks processed in parallel | Affects GPU utilization and throughput |\n| Language Pairs | Different source/target language combinations | Tests model's capabilities across languages |\n\nSources: `docs/Le_Petit_Prince_ASE.eng-Latn.T2L.txt`\n\n## 6. Translation Validation\n\n### 6.1 Validation Workflow\n\n```mermaid\nflowchart LR\n    original[\"Original Text\"]\n    translated[\"Translated Text\"]\n    backTranslated[\"Back-Translated Text\"]\n    \n    original --\u003e|\"Forward Translation\"| translated\n    translated --\u003e|\"Reverse Translation\"| backTranslated\n    \n    backTranslated \u003c--\u003e|\"Compare Similarity\"| original\n    \n    subgraph \"Validation Process\"\n        direction TB\n        similarity[\"Semantic Similarity Check\"]\n        correctness[\"Grammatical Correctness\"]\n        completeness[\"Content Completeness\"]\n    end\n    \n    original --\u003e similarity\n    backTranslated --\u003e similarity\n    translated --\u003e correctness\n    translated --\u003e completeness\n```\n\n### 6.2 Comparison with Reference Translations\n\nThe sample translated files can serve as reference translations for validation:\n\n1. Compare system outputs with reference translations\n2. Identify discrepancies or improvements\n3. Track translation quality over time\n\n## 7. Creating New Test Cases\n\nTo create new test cases using the sample files:\n\n1. Select an appropriate sample file based on testing needs\n2. Run translation with specific parameters to test\n3. Compare the output with expected results\n4. Document findings and any issues discovered\n\n### 7.1 Recommended Test Matrix\n\n| Test Scenario | Sample File | Target Language | Parameters | Expected Outcome |\n|---------------|-------------|----------------|------------|------------------|\n| Basic translation | Le_Lievre_et_la_Tortue.txt | eng_Latn | Default | Coherent English fable |\n| Long-form content | Le_Petit_Prince_ASE.eng-Latn.T2L.txt | fra_Latn | Chunk size: 512 | Match original French |\n| Memory efficiency | Le_Petit_Prince_ASE.eng-Latn.T2L.txt | deu_Latn | Batch size: 8 | Complete without OOM errors |\n| Auto-detection | Le_Lievre_et_la_Tortue.txt | spa_Latn | No source language | Correctly identify French source |\n\nSources: `docs/Le_Lievre_et_la_Tortue.txt`, `docs/Le_Petit_Prince_ASE.eng-Latn.T2L.txt`\n\n## 8. Automated Testing\n\nFor continuous integration and automated testing, the sample files can be integrated into test scripts:\n\n```bash\n# Example automated test script using sample files\nfor file in docs/*.txt; do\n  if [[ $file != *T2L.txt ]]; then\n    uv run cli-nllb.py \"$file\" -l eng_Latn -o \"${file%.txt}.eng-Latn.T2L.txt\"\n    # Add validation code here\n  fi\ndone\n```\n\n## Conclusion\n\nThe sample files included in the L2T repository provide valuable resources for testing and validating the translation system. By using these files with the provided testing utilities, developers and users can ensure proper functionality across different languages, content types, and system configurations.\n\nFor more information about system performance optimization, see [Performance Optimization](#5)."])</script><script>self.__next_f.push([1,"25:T2420,"])</script><script>self.__next_f.push([1,"# Development Guidelines\n\n\u003cdetails\u003e\n\u003csummary\u003eRelevant source files\u003c/summary\u003e\n\nThe following files were used as context for generating this wiki page:\n\n- [.gitignore](.gitignore)\n- [pyproject.toml](pyproject.toml)\n- [uv.lock](uv.lock)\n\n\u003c/details\u003e\n\n\n\nThis document provides essential information for developers who want to contribute to or modify the L2T (Language 2 Translate) system. For general usage instructions, see [Command-Line Interface](#3) and [Core Components](#4).\n\n## 1. Development Environment Setup\n\n### 1.1 Prerequisites\n\nL2T requires Python 3.13 or higher. Clone the repository:\n   ```bash\n   git clone https://github.com/OlivierLAVAUD/L2T\n   cd L2T\n   ```\n\n2. Create a virtual environment:\n   ```bash\n   python -m venv .venv\n   source .venv/bin/activate  # On Windows: .venv\\Scripts\\activate\n   ```\n\n3. Coding Standards\n\n### 3.1 Python Style Guidelines\n\nFollow these general Python coding standards:\n\n1. Use PEP 8 for code style\n2. Use meaningful variable and function names\n3. Include docstrings for all classes and functions\n4. Keep functions and methods focused on a single responsibility\n5. Use type hints where appropriate\n\nExample docstring format:\n```python\ndef function_name(param1: type, param2: type) -\u003e return_type:\n    \"\"\"\n    Brief function description.\n    \n    Longer description if needed.\n    \n    Args:\n        param1: Description of param1\n        param2: Description of param2\n        \n    Returns:\n        Description of return value\n        \n    Raises:\n        ExceptionType: When and why this exception might be raised\n    \"\"\"\n```\n\n### 3.2 Error Handling\n\nFollow these guidelines for error handling:\n\n1. Provide user-friendly error messages through the CLI\n\n```mermaid\nflowchart TD\n    subgraph \"Error Handling Flow\"\n        ui[\"User Interface\"]\n        app_code[\"Application Code\"]\n        logging[\"Logging System\"]\n        \n        app_code --\u003e|\"Raises Exception\"| try_catch{\"Try/Catch Block\"}\n        try_catch --\u003e|\"Log Error\"| logging\n        try_catch --\u003e|\"User-friendly Message\"| ui\n    end\n```\n\n## 4. Development Workflow\n\n### 4.1 Version Control\n\n1. Work in feature branches named according to the feature being implemented\n2. Keep commits small and focused\n3. Write meaningful commit messages\n4. Ensure all tests pass before submitting a pull request\n\n### 4.2 Testing Guidelines\n\nCreate tests for:\n\n1. New features\n2. Bug fixes\n3. Edge cases\n\nTest different input types:\n- Various language combinations\n- Text with special characters\n- Very large documents\n- Various file formats\n\n### 4.3 Performance Considerations\n\nWhen modifying the codebase, consider:\n\n1. Memory usage, especially for large documents\n2. Processing speed and optimization\n3. GPU utilization where applicable\n4. Resource release after processing\n\n## 5. Technical Architecture\n\n### 5.1 Core Classes and Their Relationships\n\n```mermaid\nclassDiagram\n    class TranslationCLI {\n        +run()\n        -_parse_arguments()\n        -_validate_arguments()\n        -_load_content()\n        -_translate_content()\n        -_handle_output()\n    }\n    \n    class NLLBTranslator {\n        +translate(text, source_lang, target_lang)\n        +translate_batch(texts, source_lang, target_lang)\n        +get_supported_languages()\n        -_load_model()\n    }\n    \n    class FileHandler {\n        +read_file(file_path, encoding)\n        +write_output(content, output_path)\n        -_read_pdf(file_path)\n        -_read_text_file(file_path, encoding)\n    }\n    \n    class TextProcessor {\n        +chunk_text(text, chunk_size)\n        +split_paragraphs(text)\n    }\n    \n    class ProgressHandler {\n        +display_progress(current, total)\n    }\n    \n    TranslationCLI --\u003e NLLBTranslator: uses\n    TranslationCLI --\u003e FileHandler: uses\n    TranslationCLI --\u003e TextProcessor: uses\n    TranslationCLI --\u003e ProgressHandler: uses\n```\n\nSources: Repository overview\n\n### 5.2 Translation Process Flow\n\n```mermaid\nsequenceDiagram\n    participant User\n    participant CLI as \"TranslationCLI\"\n    participant FH as \"FileHandler\"\n    participant TP as \"TextProcessor\"\n    participant NLT as \"NLLBTranslator\"\n    \n    User-\u003e\u003eCLI: Input file/text + arguments\n    CLI-\u003e\u003eCLI: Parse and validate arguments\n    \n    alt is file input\n        CLI-\u003e\u003eFH: read_file(file_path)\n        FH--\u003e\u003eCLI: content\n    end\n    \n    CLI-\u003e\u003eTP: chunk_text(content)\n    TP--\u003e\u003eCLI: chunked_text\n    \n    loop for each chunk\n        CLI-\u003e\u003eNLT: translate(chunk)\n        NLT--\u003e\u003eCLI: translated_chunk\n    end\n    \n    CLI-\u003e\u003eCLI: Combine translated chunks\n    \n    alt output to file\n        CLI-\u003e\u003eFH: write_output(translated_content)\n    else output to console\n        CLI-\u003e\u003eUser: Display translated text\n    end\n```\n\nSources: Repository overview\n\n## 6. Contributing Guidelines\n\n### 6.1 Submitting Changes\n\n1. Create a feature branch from the main branch\n2. Implement your changes\n3. Add or update tests as needed\n4. Ensure all tests pass\n5. Submit a pull request with a clear description of the changes\n\n### 6.2 Code Review Process\n\nCode reviews will focus on:\n\n1. Correctness - does the code work as intended?\n2. Troubleshooting Common Development Issues\n\n### 7.1 Model Loading Issues\n\n- Ensure sufficient disk space for model files\n- Check internet connection for initial model download\n- Verify GPU compatibility if using GPU acceleration\n\n### 7.2 Performance Debugging\n\nFor performance issues:\n\n1. Use chunking for large texts\n2. Set appropriate batch sizes for GPU memory\n3. Monitor memory usage during processing\n4.
